  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_de5f90c3-da2a-4916-a442-3675d3bfb11d'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer18356003520769695910">Francis Chisholm is a compassionate and humble priest whose individuality and directness make him unpopular with other clergy. Considered a failure by his superiors, he is sent to China to maintain a mission amid desperate poverty, civil war, plague, and the hostility of his superiors.   <span id="freeText18356003520769695910" style="display:none">Francis Chisholm is a compassionate and humble priest whose individuality and directness make him unpopular with other clergy. Considered a failure by his superiors, he is sent to China to maintain a mission amid desperate poverty, civil war, plague, and the hostility of his superiors. In the face of this constant danger and hardship, Father Chisholm finds the keys to the kingdom of heaven. Recognized as A. J. Cronin’s best novel, <i>The Keys of the Kingdom </i>is an enthralling, fast-moving, colorful tale of a deeply spiritual man called to do good in an imperfect world.<br />  </span>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/43933937-paula-soto"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1434230405i/43933937._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/43933937-paula-soto">Paula Soto</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">L'enfer s'il existe est réservée à ceux qui n'ont pas réussi à trouver la grâce dans leur vie. À ceux qui n'ont su ni aimer, ni apprécier la beauté de<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">L'enfer s'il existe est réservée à ceux qui n'ont pas réussi à trouver la grâce dans leur vie. À ceux qui n'ont su ni aimer, ni apprécier la beauté de la vie, à ceux qui n'ont jamais su prêter la main aux plus faibles ni pardonner les offences passées et ni aidé à construire des instants de bonheur. En bref s'il y a un enfer il est réservé à ceux qui ont refusé de vivre la vie.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2142472821" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2142472821" />
    <a title="Fergus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70395042-fergus"><img alt="Fergus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567548184p2/70395042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2142472821?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fergus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fergus" href="/user/show/70395042-fergus">Fergus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25513058-the-keys-of-the-kingdom">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2142472821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11412245283922381781">It’s NEVER over!<br/><br/>When I was 13 years old, my wonderfully wise grandmother came to live with us. <br/><br/>My parents had turned me and my younger siblings into the pampered offspring of a double-income, upwardly-mobile fifties family 6 years previous to this, and the plans for their proud acquisition of a new and modern split-level home - when I turned thirteen - had had enough gracious foresight to provide an ensuite apartment for my grandmother.<br/><br/>“Gagi”, as I had brokenly mispronounced the word Granny at 1</span>
  <span id="freeText11412245283922381781" style="display:none">It’s NEVER over!<br /><br />When I was 13 years old, my wonderfully wise grandmother came to live with us. <br /><br />My parents had turned me and my younger siblings into the pampered offspring of a double-income, upwardly-mobile fifties family 6 years previous to this, and the plans for their proud acquisition of a new and modern split-level home - when I turned thirteen - had had enough gracious foresight to provide an ensuite apartment for my grandmother.<br /><br />“Gagi”, as I had brokenly mispronounced the word Granny at 18 months, had stuck as her revered sobriquet. And each visit she made to our previous little bungalow, before the big move that summer, had been for me like Alice following the March Hare into Wonderland.<br /><br />She always had fantastically imaginative stories to tell us kids! And that’s not all - for that magical summer of the move, after she came... her THOUSANDS of books were soon to follow her - in a huge Moving Van.<br /><br />That same van included furniture, artwork and antiques. Many of those were irreparably damaged in the long haul from central Utah. Strangely, that was inconsequential to the young, spoilt kid I was. <br /><br />For her BOOKS arrived in mint condition! <br /><br />That summer I PORED over them gluttonously.<br /><br />She must have seen the gleam in my eyes, for in her will she bequeathed them all to me! And when my wife and I made the big move to OUR house in 1984, my Dad passed them on to us. And THIS - this was the first old book I unpacked - and then READ voraciously, cover to cover. <br /><br />For I was now Catholic, and recognized Francis Chisholm’s Dark Night of the Soul as my own!<br /><br />Yes! And this story of a shiningly idealistic young Scottish priest made a HUGE impression on me. Francis - yeah, right, sounds like Fergus - Chisholm is idealistic, but he has one ACHILLES HEEL: he says whatever’s on his mind, no matter how awful it sounds. <br /><br />Like I always did - the same thing. Come heck or high water. I could relate, as you’ll soon see...<br />***<br /><br />It was a stressful day seven years later.<br /><br />All Heck arrived on my doorstop. And just like Father Chisholm’s long, forced purgatory in China, it took me down a few pivotal pegs!<br /><br />QUITE a few. Right down the Rabbit Hole, in fact.<br /><br />Then, later on, again - when 1991 came, the free world was basking in the reflected Glory of Glasnost. <br /><br />And I?<br /><br />I was chomping at the bit with suppressed fury at the clubbish oligarchy of a few clannish old boys that ruled my then-current privileged position. <br /><br />Because privilege has its hard and fast obligations. And I was a free spirit.<br /><br />So - VERY unwisely - that day I pulled a Pierre Élliott Trudeau and quite uncouthly told my boss to fuddle duddle, if you remember that historical vignette. Google it if you don’t.<br /><br />Stark silence greeted me. <br /><br />Then ALL of hell’s fury broke open.<br /><br />Within three working days I was dropped from my privileged (and upwardly mobile?) middle management platform, to a kick-butt sweatshop of an office supervising a small but defiantly opinionated cadre of clerks.<br /><br />I (again, unwisely? Yet still honestly) let it be widely known that I was quite pleased with my challenging new rôle - and would never again demean myself by such a surge toward rapid promotion. <br /><br />Some would say I was pretty dumb. I simply thought myself honest.<br /><br />But in coming clean I wiped my star-rated career slate clean, as well. At least I no longer had dirty hands. I had broken free.<br /><br />And now had to prove myself ALL OVER AGAIN.<br /><br />Now, did my dear grandmother’s A.J. Cronin novel lead me to THAT?<br /><br />Well, our Maker works in circuitously serendipitous ways, and I don’t know much about serendipity, but I do know life can be awfully rum, as one of Stephen Dedalus’ buddies said.<br /><br />And you know what else?<br /><br />If Father Chisholm could buck ecclesiastical authority and STILL find a home in Glory...<br /><br />Maybe there was still hope for me! And...<br /><br />With a few EXTRA points for outraged ingenuousness, perhaps?<br /><br />Haha. I know, fat chance.<br /><br />That final, burnt-out year, still a middle manager, I was awarded the Queen’s Golden Jubilee Medal. <br /><br />But I was FAR from being ALONE in that honour. Many, MANY more were also awarded it in the Jubilee year.<br /><br />Many, Much More Deserving, Thousands of Canadians -<br /><br />But at least... I had given it my Best Shot!<br /><br />I can say that now honestly.<br /><br />What stuck with me most about that day, and after all these years I remember them, I still feel their effect...<br /><br />Were the words our tough-as-nails DG, Gord Hunter, said to me at that moment he put the gold medal on my sagging chest:<br /><br />“That’s Fantastic, Fergus. You’ve earned it - and I REALLY Mean That!”<br /><br />Like, you know what I mean?<br /><br />Like a Million Dollars...<br /><br />And just like Father Chisholm, at the end of this book:<br /><br />I had won a Pyrrhic Victory.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11412245283922381781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16744785089971289792">A colleague and friend recently reminded me of the movie of this book in 1944 that starred Gregory Peck. It got me to thinking that it has been easily forty years since I read any A.J. Cronin.<br/><br/>Loyola Press is to be commended for including this novel by A.J. Cronin in its list of Loyola Classics. Cronin (1896-1981) is sadly forgotten today, but I recall in my youth the buzz at my local public library whenever a new book by Cronin appeared.<br/><br/>Three of his better novels, Keys of the Kingdom, The Stars </span>
  <span id="freeText16744785089971289792" style="display:none">A colleague and friend recently reminded me of the movie of this book in 1944 that starred Gregory Peck. It got me to thinking that it has been easily forty years since I read any A.J. Cronin.<br /><br />Loyola Press is to be commended for including this novel by A.J. Cronin in its list of Loyola Classics. Cronin (1896-1981) is sadly forgotten today, but I recall in my youth the buzz at my local public library whenever a new book by Cronin appeared.<br /><br />Three of his better novels, Keys of the Kingdom, The Stars Look Down, and The Citadel made successful transitions to the silver screen and are considered classics of their era.<br /><br />The figure of Father Francis Chisholm, from his poverty-stricken childhood in the 1870s, through a ministry (largely in China as a missionary from the end of the 19th century until the eve of World War II) perceived by his peers as mediocre, to his old age and retirement, is one that is not easily forgotten. Some of his universalist bromides would most definitely been out of place in the Roman Catholic Church at the time, but Fr. Chisholm is the kind of maverick many of us cannot help but admire.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16744785089971289792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15785409834467517730">This is probably the most significant book I've ever read. It has shaped who I am and how I approach life more than any other book. I have a very old copy from my grandmother that I reread whenever I feel the need to do a little soul searching.<br/><br/>The book description doesn't do it justice. I strongly recommend it. It is not, not, not a book that tries to convert you to any particular religious belief (the main character is a priest, but his best friend is an atheist, and the main character is sure </span>
  <span id="freeText15785409834467517730" style="display:none">This is probably the most significant book I've ever read. It has shaped who I am and how I approach life more than any other book. I have a very old copy from my grandmother that I reread whenever I feel the need to do a little soul searching.<br /><br />The book description doesn't do it justice. I strongly recommend it. It is not, not, not a book that tries to convert you to any particular religious belief (the main character is a priest, but his best friend is an atheist, and the main character is sure that there are Buddists in heaven). And, the character could be anyone, which is amazing since most people wouldn't relate to a priest to a good representation of all humankind, but the guy isn't sitting around saying, I'm a priest, therefore... He's saying, I think this is the only way to show love to others, therefore...<br /><br />It's a heavy book, but it's wonderful.</span>

Why?!<br/>There are two categories of books, Books and "The books", The Keys Of The Kingdom belongs to "The books" category..<br/>A.J.   <span id="freeText3942531392341706791" style="display:none">Why did it have to end?! Why?!<br />There are two categories of books, Books and "The books", The Keys Of The Kingdom belongs to "The books" category..<br />A.J. Cronin, took us to different places, diffrent states of mind and diffrent moods, through happy times, cruel situations, heartbreaking events, terror moments, made us smile, get angry and weep..<br />It's Francis Chicholm, one of the most amazing characters I've ever met, the incarnation of humanity, dignity and sacrifice..<br />From being mistreated in England by his relatives after the death of his parents to his aunt Polly's arms where he felt much happier to Hollywell religious school, then comes china, where he went as a missionary to Pai Tan, a lost spot with no hope.. There he faced ignorance, plague, nature, wars.. he had been wounded, but he stayed humble, to the end, a pure spirit who always gives and never waits for anything in return.. This was a little resumé, a lot of things happened, the kinda stuff that gets you glued to the book, yes, this is the kinda books you cannot put down, I remember my sister suggesting it, I started it few years ago but left it after few pages.. one thing is sure, I almost missed one of the best books I've ever read!</span>

<div id="review_696282584" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/696282584" />
    <a title="Vishwanath Praveen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12820914-vishwanath-praveen"><img alt="Vishwanath Praveen" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/696282584?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vishwanath Praveen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vishwanath Praveen" href="/user/show/12820914-vishwanath-praveen">Vishwanath Praveen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer696282584" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10809618253294463544">"Have a heart that never hardens, and a temper that never tires and a touch that never hurts" - Charles Dickens<br/>Not sure if Dickens had written a prelude to Father Francis Chisholm's character, but this quote symbolises what the protagonist in A.J.Cronin's beautifully written novel "Keys of the Kingdom" stood for.<br/>This proved to be one of the most un-putdownable non-mystery/thriller books for me. I think the book is a biography of Cronin's friend(to whom this book is dedicated) who was a missionar</span>
  <span id="freeText10809618253294463544" style="display:none">"Have a heart that never hardens, and a temper that never tires and a touch that never hurts" - Charles Dickens<br />Not sure if Dickens had written a prelude to Father Francis Chisholm's character, but this quote symbolises what the protagonist in A.J.Cronin's beautifully written novel "Keys of the Kingdom" stood for.<br />This proved to be one of the most un-putdownable non-mystery/thriller books for me. I think the book is a biography of Cronin's friend(to whom this book is dedicated) who was a missionary in China for 20 years. It chronicles the life of Father Francis Chisholm right from his young days in Scotland to his years as an unconventional Catholic priest who struggles to setup a mission in China. His ecclesiastical methods(sometimes borderline blasphemous) are always debated by his peers leading to a parish investigation after his return to Scotland from the mission after 20 years. But his deeds outweigh the methods and he eventually comes out unscathed.<br />The underlying theme of the book is the resilience of the human spirit as demonstrated by the main character. Despite innumerable personal tragedies that he encounters during the course of his life, Father Chisholm always stands up for what he believes is the ultimate truth, that humanity is above all religions. His spontaneous goodness rather than his position as a religious man strike a chord with people he meets.<br />The narrative flows seamlessly from the beginning to the end. Almost all characters in the novel are well developed but the ones that stood out barring Father Francis were Aunt Polly and the German nun Mother Maria-Veronica.<br />One might wonder about the seemingly conspicuous absence of 'grey' shades that are quintissential in a human being.But again there lies the strength of Cronin's writing. The Father does have shades of grey like firmly believing in what is right and doing the right thing at the cost of moral conflicts with himself.<br />What moved me the most was the Father's strikingly 'human' nature, one that was bereft of holy pretensions.<br />I wouldn't want to delve into any part of the plot and spoil the joy of discovering this wonderful classic that Cronin has so artfully crafted. But I can say with certainty that Father Francis Chisholm is sure to go down as one of the most loved characters in the annals of literary history.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10809618253294463544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Kris, Christianne, Michelle, Helen</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1803215014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7435968670595007923"> I was ready for a book recommended for "innate goodness" and this worked! I would probably have scored it a 4.5, but I am rating up for the lasting value of this novel. A dear Russian friend recommended it as one of her all time favorite English reads. It did take me a little while to get caught-up in it. I felt at the beginning like I was revisiting Dicken's young Pip or David Copperfield. The setting and background were stark and the people indigent, but the trials and tribulations forged a m</span>
  <span id="freeText7435968670595007923" style="display:none"> I was ready for a book recommended for "innate goodness" and this worked! I would probably have scored it a 4.5, but I am rating up for the lasting value of this novel. A dear Russian friend recommended it as one of her all time favorite English reads. It did take me a little while to get caught-up in it. I felt at the beginning like I was revisiting Dicken's young Pip or David Copperfield. The setting and background were stark and the people indigent, but the trials and tribulations forged a most forgiving and sensitive main character.<br /><br /> Once this maverick minister landed in China the story definitely soared for me. This visionary man cared. The poverty of his childhood perhaps enabled him to adapt and to optimistically find a way to help his new community. I found myself with pen in hand generously underlining passages and even beliefs. His religion was not based on dogma but rather on humility, kindness and a belief that you can look for and find good in diverse places and with diverse people. He would be just as likely to quote Buddha as St. Paul.<br /><br /> I wish I still had the book to reference, but I have already shared it with a granddaughter. Truthfully, I confess that the end brought tears. That is unusual for me. The characters are strong and they grow. The book was uplifting and my take-away is that I want to strive to be a better and kinder person. I choose love. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7435968670595007923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152211122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16530903342883955656">I read this book at 14 so here's my memory:<br/><br/>A romantic view of a dedicated man who surrenders everything to serve God (and later be well-played by Gregory Peck). He goes to China, and is beloved by all but the Mother Superior with whom he serves God. But in the end she has to respect his dedication and integrity. He is intellectually gifted but sometimes pragmatically challenged & quirky and although he inadvertently flies in the face of Catholic authorities because of his true holiness they (as </span>
  <span id="freeText16530903342883955656" style="display:none">I read this book at 14 so here's my memory:<br /><br />A romantic view of a dedicated man who surrenders everything to serve God (and later be well-played by Gregory Peck). He goes to China, and is beloved by all but the Mother Superior with whom he serves God. But in the end she has to respect his dedication and integrity. He is intellectually gifted but sometimes pragmatically challenged &amp; quirky and although he inadvertently flies in the face of Catholic authorities because of his true holiness they (as of course Catholic authorities do so often!) forgive him his trespasses because they admire his honesty.<br /><br />He is a wonderfully drawn character &amp; a great ad for priesthood and Roman Catholicism. It was also the perfect way for me to begin to enter the history of China in the early-mid 20th century.<br /><br />I don't remember the prose style, but I read it with ease at 14. I loved the descriptions of the small Welsh village the Father comes from as well as rural China and relished being transported into completely different cultures, both early-20th century (or late 19th century?) Wales and rural China. <br /><br />I learned a lot (and if I remember correctly, the information presented was factually accurate) and enjoyed myself enormously.<br /><br />Of course, I'm a very romantic Roman Catholic kind of girl.</span>

          </span>

    <a title="Nelleke Plouffe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23900493-nelleke-plouffe"><img alt="Nelleke Plouffe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379021483p2/23900493.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/22277715-the-keys-of-the-kingdom">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2739433136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7492495924802736479">Once again Cronin does not disappoint. While I do not agree with the universalism preached in this book, it is still a beautiful picture of the value of personal integrity, and of Christ-like loving and giving of self. I highly recommend this author.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2739433136">
  <td colspan="2">

<span id="freeTextContainer14796417127412863939">I loved this book when I first read it back in October 2007. Rereading it eight years later I am somewhat less enamored. It's still an excellent story about an amazingly selfless British priest who serves in China at the beginning of the 20th century. Despite the title and main character, the book is ecumenical, although it does tend to be a bit romantic. <br/><br/>Worthwhile read. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3348465938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17656739002673163867">Thought to be Cronin's best novel, I picked it up because it had so influenced a Goodreads reviewer that I follow -<br/><br/>This is a pre-modern book. Meaning it's a story, with a main character, easy to read, many things happen, the hero grows up and into his good heart. People struggle to exist in a world that is cruel and always on the brink of war, horror, starvation, plague.<br/><br/>Father Chisholm, a Catholic priest sent to a mission in China, does good things in a landscape of poverty. Although the idea of</span>
  <span id="freeText17656739002673163867" style="display:none">Thought to be Cronin's best novel, I picked it up because it had so influenced a Goodreads reviewer that I follow -<br /><br />This is a pre-modern book. Meaning it's a story, with a main character, easy to read, many things happen, the hero grows up and into his good heart. People struggle to exist in a world that is cruel and always on the brink of war, horror, starvation, plague.<br /><br />Father Chisholm, a Catholic priest sent to a mission in China, does good things in a landscape of poverty. Although the idea of missionaries is currently pretty reprehensible (at least to me) the good priest is a good man and his life is given to good deeds and self sacrifice. I can see how a young spiritual-leaning reader could find him to be a beacon to follow (I myself loved The Nun's Story - notwithstanding I was not a Catholic!)<br /><br />For many the world is yet cruel. Maybe it's growing more that way. Perhaps we will need Father Chisholm. That being said, did he save anyone's soul other than his own? Not sure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17656739002673163867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3309065102" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12357152813737252499">Initially the story seemed rather uninteresting, but towards the end it became more able to capture my attention, and I found myself less able to put it down. In the start of the novel, Francis Chisholm seems either too tragic or too angelic, making this main character difficult to know deeply. But when he is Father Chisholm in China amongst combating warlords, then he comes to life. <br/><br/>The writing sometimes seemed too understated or opaque for me to follow turns of the plot. I would have to go bac</span>
  <span id="freeText12357152813737252499" style="display:none">Initially the story seemed rather uninteresting, but towards the end it became more able to capture my attention, and I found myself less able to put it down. In the start of the novel, Francis Chisholm seems either too tragic or too angelic, making this main character difficult to know deeply. But when he is Father Chisholm in China amongst combating warlords, then he comes to life. <br /><br />The writing sometimes seemed too understated or opaque for me to follow turns of the plot. I would have to go back and read a page to make sure I really understood what took place. <br /><br />In terms of faith, Fr. Chisholm seems to hit a balance able to disturb traditionalists and progressives alike. He leans a little too far toward universalism for me, but at the same time he emphasizes true spiritual growth and devotion above changes on a social level, thus upsetting those who emphasize measurable results and social progress - the type that want to implement the latest management styles to the cause of world missions. He is extremely likable to this reader, the kind of foreign missionary who would be both a pleasure and a frustration with whom to work.<br /><br />Very glad I attained this book back in 2010 somehow, and sorry it took me a decade to get to it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12357152813737252499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12336316232648081546">I must emotionally feel this is one of the few great novels I have read. This book was written by A.J.Cronin in 1941. It starts with a young priest in the British Isles. His name is Father Francis Chisholm, a Scottish priest who is somewhat unconventional in his methods. If I tried to pick out his methods I would say spreading love, and his desire is to establish a mission in China. As you read through his adventures you see the Chinese people, from the most poor to warlords to the heads of othe</span>
  <span id="freeText12336316232648081546" style="display:none">I must emotionally feel this is one of the few great novels I have read. This book was written by A.J.Cronin in 1941. It starts with a young priest in the British Isles. His name is Father Francis Chisholm, a Scottish priest who is somewhat unconventional in his methods. If I tried to pick out his methods I would say spreading love, and his desire is to establish a mission in China. As you read through his adventures you see the Chinese people, from the most poor to warlords to the heads of other denominations in China finding this humble man with his kindly and loving ways creating his mission but also establishing a mutual understanding and respect among all with each other. In ends with his being returned to Scotland and being joined with his friends of old. Please read it, you deserve it. If you have read it then read it again.</span>

<div id="review_1720679332" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1720679332" />
    <a title="Penney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14584770-penney"><img alt="Penney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485045181p2/14584770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1720679332?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penney" href="/user/show/14584770-penney">Penney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1720679332" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13568728014890849984">Even though I'm not Catholic, I somehow stumbled into the Loyola Classics series, and this novel from that collection made a deep impression on me. The philosophy conveyed is far from dogmatic--in fact, quite the opposite. Father Francis is one of those literary characters who will stay with me in memory just as strongly as people I have known in the "real" world. This narrative of one man's patience, humility, determination, honesty, endurance, compassion, tolerance, commonsense, and courage is</span>
  <span id="freeText13568728014890849984" style="display:none">Even though I'm not Catholic, I somehow stumbled into the Loyola Classics series, and this novel from that collection made a deep impression on me. The philosophy conveyed is far from dogmatic--in fact, quite the opposite. Father Francis is one of those literary characters who will stay with me in memory just as strongly as people I have known in the "real" world. This narrative of one man's patience, humility, determination, honesty, endurance, compassion, tolerance, commonsense, and courage is, quite simply, inspirational.</span>

<div id="review_2481376663" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2481376663" />
    <a title="Tarissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2630602-tarissa"><img alt="Tarissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370317755p2/2630602.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2481376663?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tarissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tarissa" href="/user/show/2630602-tarissa">Tarissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2481376663" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7769975895045444536">A moving story, that helps you to grow as a person as you flip each page.<br/><br/>Francis Chisholm's life is separated into two parts, it seems to me. There was his happy childhood and the love of his life who could not be his; then on to becoming a dedicated Catholic priest and missionary.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>“....I must record this inescapable sense of belonging to God, which strikes at me through the darkness, the deep conviction....”</b>
</i><br/><br/>I love the details of his life. The story told how he would venture to the church in </span>
  <span id="freeText7769975895045444536" style="display:none">A moving story, that helps you to grow as a person as you flip each page.<br /><br />Francis Chisholm's life is separated into two parts, it seems to me. There was his happy childhood and the love of his life who could not be his; then on to becoming a dedicated Catholic priest and missionary.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“....I must record this inescapable sense of belonging to God, which strikes at me through the darkness, the deep conviction....”</b>
</i><br /><br />I love the details of his life. The story told how he would venture to the church in the nighttime to pray, and peace would overwhelm him. There are great points in the plot showing how he strives to touch people in the heart. He's not the kind of priest to bring people in by the boatloads and have slackers and dishonestly “saved” people in his congregation. No, he worked hard to save each individual soul, by faith, through God's grace, and with his “good Scot's sense”. Even in China, for thirty-five years where he steadfastly worked, where he is faced with miserable circumstances, those same principles keep guiding him.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Will you young idiots kindly stop treating me like your great-grandmother on her hundredth birthday?”</b>
</i><br /><br /><b>For the discerning/Christian reader:</b> There are a couple of instances where “adult” content is alluded too. Very brief, not much. Also, there are some references to bits of theology that are not sound doctrine – but I let it pass because Chisholm is a wonderful priest regardless.<br /><br /><b>The bottom line?</b> Francis Chisholm is a missionary of valor. I found his story, fiction though it is, to be abounding with incredible-ness and awe-inspiring encouragement. <br /><br />Oh, and another thing... After finishing the book, go back and read chapter 1. I found that it fills in the ending so well. In fact, it's the real ending.<br /><br />Possibly my favorite quote of the whole book, due to the comical reaction I get every time I read it:<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Oh, Lord, for once – not thy will, but mine, be done.” </b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7769975895045444536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3073272064" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3073272064" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9784757-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471992670p2/9784757.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3073272064?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/9784757-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3073272064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14344449299139239812">I had never heard of this book, but it was amazing. It was the simple story of a Scottish priest and yet it was powerful. It starts in the 1890's when he is 7. His father is assaulted for his religious beliefs. When his mother tries to rescue him, they are both drowned and Francis is now an orphan. He moves around to different families and eventually goes to a Catholic boarding school. <br/><br/>His decision to become a priest is complex and his views are unorthodox. He struggles to fit in with the other </span>
  <span id="freeText14344449299139239812" style="display:none">I had never heard of this book, but it was amazing. It was the simple story of a Scottish priest and yet it was powerful. It starts in the 1890's when he is 7. His father is assaulted for his religious beliefs. When his mother tries to rescue him, they are both drowned and Francis is now an orphan. He moves around to different families and eventually goes to a Catholic boarding school. <br /><br />His decision to become a priest is complex and his views are unorthodox. He struggles to fit in with the other priests and is eventually assigned as a missionary in China. There is no mission, no converts, and no money. But Father Francis prevails.<br /><br />He was a good man and you feel all the different emotions. There is happiness, there is anger, and there is his faith. I really enjoyed it. I felt frustrated with certain characters when they were annoying and shared in joy with others. I like those books that you get enmeshed with everyone.<br /><br />There was a point where Father Francis and his party were kidnapped and it was interesting and then suddenly he was back in his mission. I didn't like the skipping over the solution to it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14344449299139239812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_671964849" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/671964849" />
    <a title="Patty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2616893-patty"><img alt="Patty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307135013p2/2616893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/671964849?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patty" href="/user/show/2616893-patty">Patty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer671964849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14901212274380563248">A.J. Cronin has to be the most under-recognized author in history. In the hands of a lesser writer, Keys might have been a sappy, dated novel, but I believe it has truly stood the test of time. Cronin achieved vivid descriptions, depth of characters and exciting adventure to create a story I couldn't put down. Father Chisholm was an inspiration and I miss him now that I've finished the book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/5559570-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316161657" href="/book/show/7719395-the-keys-of-the-kingdom">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5559570-james?shelf=christianity">christianity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5559570-james?shelf=history">history</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer375431174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13787645632154270191">My dad gave this book to me as a result of finding it on a beach trip. I enjoyed this book even though it was hard to follow at times -- perhaps because I took so long to read it. Regardless, I greatly admired Father Chisolm's perseverance. That is a reminder to me that whenever I'm in dire straits, all I have to do is let God know that I need His help. And who knows? Perhaps someday I'll travel out of this country for missions purposes because I think Cronin, in some ways, has inspired me to do</span>
  <span id="freeText13787645632154270191" style="display:none">My dad gave this book to me as a result of finding it on a beach trip. I enjoyed this book even though it was hard to follow at times -- perhaps because I took so long to read it. Regardless, I greatly admired Father Chisolm's perseverance. That is a reminder to me that whenever I'm in dire straits, all I have to do is let God know that I need His help. And who knows? Perhaps someday I'll travel out of this country for missions purposes because I think Cronin, in some ways, has inspired me to do so. I've had the desire to and will definitely do so Lord willing. Cronin kept me interested all the way through with his engaging dialogue and vivid descriptions. All in all, I'm glad I read the book since it was long but rewarding.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13787645632154270191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_37112722" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37112722" />
    <a title="Kristen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/602124-kristen"><img alt="Kristen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285362410p2/602124.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37112722?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/602124-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37112722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13857713650662019378">This is a beautiful book in the style of <u>How Green Was My Valley</u> describing the life of a young man growing up in Scotland and becoming a Catholic priest. He is sent to an out-of-the-way town in China under the impression that he is taking over a well-established mission. This book resonated with me because of its Kierkegaardian philosophies about Christianity, and does a great job of taking on the issues of religion vs. morality without being preachy or sentimental. A great read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wGBNr20gZ8nwKmaMFbOdL1SYN38TXmV+7gLTSChleYuY6TeShXYUpFmpkK4zvgc8Fc36Po0mPDAvgYAbKJniPw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('t1T1cnZCPIzMOjWexOgQFjAsW49VvDRx0K48MgjbgvTv3Y9PnhRP4WW5w7zi5YoFcXmWzsvEbT8RLW9hCCcZQA==')})
  }

But at what cost? Now, as China closes the book on the policy after over three decades, it faces a population grown too old and too male, with a vastly diminished supply of young workers. \n\nMei Fong has spent years documenting the policy\'s repercussions on every sector of Chinese society. In One Child, she explores its true human impact, traveling across China to meet the people who live with its consequences. Their stories reveal a dystopian reality: unauthorized second children ignored by the state, only children supporting aging parents and grandparents on their own, villages teeming with ineligible bachelors. Fong tackles questions that have major implications for China\'s future: whether its Little Emperor cohort will make for an entitled or risk-averse generation; how China will manage to support itself when one in every four people is over sixty-five years old; and above all, how much the one-child policy may end up hindering China\'s growth. \n\nWeaving in Fong\'s reflections on striving to become By the time she was a young teenager, she was already making news and attracting attention. Taylor would go onto star in movies such as A Place in the Sun, Butterfield 8, Who\'s Afraid of Virginia Woolf?, and Cleopatra, where she played opposite Richard Burton. Her affair with Burton caused a worldwide scandal, and the movie almost ruined Twentieth Century Fox. Taylor and Burton were married and divorced twice, with the world watching their every scandalous move.\n\nIn her fifties, when Taylor was no longer in demand for leading lady roles, she developed her own brand of perfumes and jewelry. These were so successful that she made more money from her brands than from her movies. She also became the voice for AIDS when everyone else in Hollywood ignored the subject. Her grandchildren have now taken over the Elizabeth Taylor AIDS Foundation and continue her work long after her death. Elizabeth Taylor, the “most beautiful woman in the world,” will continue to affect people for years to come.\n\nDiscover a plethora of topics such as\n∙Born Beautiful\n∙Becoming Mrs. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2532287892429818387">Archibald Joseph Cronin was a Scottish novelist, dramatist, and non-fiction writer who was one of the most renowned storytellers of the twentieth century. His best-known works are <i>The Citadel</i> and <i>The Keys of the Kingdom</i>, both of which were made into Oscar-nominated films. He also created the Dr. Finlay character, the hero of a series of stories that served as the basis for the long-running BBC tel</span>
  <span id="freeText2532287892429818387" style="display:none">Archibald Joseph Cronin was a Scottish novelist, dramatist, and non-fiction writer who was one of the most renowned storytellers of the twentieth century. His best-known works are <i>The Citadel</i> and <i>The Keys of the Kingdom</i>, both of which were made into Oscar-nominated films. He also created the Dr. Finlay character, the hero of a series of stories that served as the basis for the long-running BBC television and radio series entitled Dr. Finlay's Casebook.<br />-Wikipedia: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A.J._Cronin">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A.J._Cronin</a><br /><br /></span>
